     348             : 
     349             : #if CFRONT_GLOBAL_VS_MEMBER_NAME_LOOKUP_BUG
     350             : 
     351             : static a_symbol_ptr check_for_cfront_name_lookup_bug
     352             :                                         (a_type_ptr                class_type,
     353             :                                          a_symbol_ptr              sym,
     354             :                                          a_symbol_locator          *locator,
     355             :                                          an_id_lookup_options_set  options)
     356             : /*
     357             : Cfront 2.1 has a bug that causes a global identifier to be found when
     358             : a member of a class or one of its base classes should actually be found.
     359             : The following code illustrates an instance in which the bug occurs:
     360             : 
     361             : struct B   {
     362             :         void func(const char*); // Needs to be here
     363             : };
     364             : 
     365             : struct D : public B {
     366             : public:
     367             :         D();
     368             :         void Init(const char* );
     369             : };
     370             : 
     371             : struct func {
     372             :         func( const char* msg);
     373             : };
     374             : 
     375             : D::D(){}
     376             : 
     377             : void D::Init(const char* t)
     378             : {
     379             :         new func(t);
     380             : }
     381             : 
     382             : For the bad lookup to occur:
     383             : 
     384             : 1. A member in a base class must have the same name as an identifier
     385             :    at the global scope.  Any member kind is OK -- it can be a function,
     386             :    static data member, or nonstatic data member.  Member type names don't
     387             :    apply because a nested type will be promoted to the global scope by
     388             :    cfront which disallows a later declaration of a type with the same name
     389             :    at the global scope.
     390             : 
     391             : 2. The declaration of the global scope name must occur between the declaration
     392             :    of the derived class and the declaration of either an out-of-line
     393             :    constructor or destructor.  The global scope name must be a type name.
     394             : 
     395             : 3. No other member function definition -- even one for an unrelated class
     396             :    may appear between the destructor and the offending reference.
     397             :    This has the effect that the bad lookup applies to only one class at
     398             :    any given point in time.
     399             : 
     400             : The global variable last_ctor_or_dtor_sym is set by function_declaration
     401             : when the body of a constructor or destructor that is defined outside of
     402             : the class definition is processed.  This field is cleared when any other
     403             : member function is defined.
     404             : */
     405             : {
     406             :   a_derivation_step_ptr path = NULL;
     407             :   an_access_specifier   access;
     408             :   a_boolean             ambiguous, any_using_decl;
     409             :   a_symbol_ptr          new_sym = sym;
     410             : 
     411             :   /* Before this routine is called we will have already verified that the
     412             :      lookup terminated in the class reactivation scope for the same class
     413             :      as indicated by last_ctor_or_dtor_sym.  This means that we are

    2178             :

    2180             : 
    2181             :   namespace N1 {

    2190             :   }

    2193             :   int v2;
    2194             :

    2196             :     g(v1, v2);

    3504             : /*
    3505             : When a normal lookup reaches passes reaches an instantiation scope and,
    3506             : after considering the template parameters, still has not found a symbol,
    3507             : the context of the instantiation must be considered.  The context
    3508             : has two components: the definition context (where the template was
    3509             : declared or defined) and the referencing context (the namespace containing
    3510             : the reference that caused the instantiation).
    3511             : 
    3512             : The symbol may be found in one or both of the contexts.  If the symbol is
    3513             : found in both contexts, both instances must be functions.
    3514             : 
    3515             : The two lookups are done by calling scope_stack_lookup with the
    3516             : appropriate set of starting and ending scopes.  The ending scopes
    3517             : specified will result in all scopes having been considered up to
    3518             : a "common" scope at which the two lookup paths come back together.
    3519             : The two lookups could result in zero, one, or two symbols being found.

    3521             : If one symbol is found, the search also begins with the common

    5402             : 
    5403             : static
    5404             : a_symbol_ptr qualified_using_directive_lookup(
    5405             :                         a_symbol_locator                *locator,
    5406             :                         a_namespace_ptr                 ns_ptr,
    5407             :                         a_scope_ptr                     ns_scope,
    5408             :                         an_id_lookup_options_set        options,
    5409             :                         a_namespace_ptr                 orig_ns_ptr,
    5410             :                         a_symbol_ptr                    *synth_sym,
    5411             :                         a_boolean                       *any_errors,
    5412             :                         a_boolean                       inline_namespace_only)
    5413             : /*
    5414             : Do a qualified lookup of namespaces nominated by using directives
    5415             : in this scope.  This is used for qualified namespace and file scope
    5416             : lookups.  For functions, the symbol returned may be an overload set
    5417             : containing functions from several namespaces.  For nonfunctions,
    5418             : an ambiguity may need to be diagnosed.
    5419             : 
    5420             : locator describes the symbol being looked up.  ns_scope is the namespace
    5421             : (or file scope) in which we should look for the symbol.  if ns_scope is
    5422             : a namespace, ns_ptr points to the namespace.  options are the lookup options
    5423             : to be used.  orig_ns_ptr is the namespace specified in the qualifier.
    5424             : *synth_sym points to a synthesized projection symbol that captures the
    5425             : results of the lookup.  *any_errors is set to TRUE if an ambiguity is
    5426             : detected.
    5427             : 
    5428             :          D        E
    5429             :           \      /
    5430             :            B    C
    5431             :             \  /
    5432             :              A
    5433             : 
    5434             :   namespace E { int l; }  
    5435             :   namespace D { int j, l; void g(double); }
    5436             :   namespace C { int k;    void g(char); using namespace E; }
    5437             :   namespace B { int j;    void g(int);  using namespace D; }
    5438             :   namespace A { int i;    void f();     using namespace B; using namespace C;}
    5439             : 
    5440             : A qualified lookup begins with the namespace specified by the qualifier.
    5441             : If the name is found there, the lookup stops.  If it is not found there,
    5442             : the lookup looks in each of the namespaces used in using directives in
    5443             : that namespace.  Functions from each namespace are merged together
    5444             : into an overload set.  If more than one name is found, and they are not
    5445             : all functions, the lookup is ambiguous.
    5446             : 
    5447             : Using the example above, the result of the following lookups are
    5448             : as follows:
    5449             : 
    5450             :         Lookup          Result
    5451             :         ------          ------
    5452             :         A::i            A::i
    5453             :         A::j            B::j
    5454             :         A::k            C::k
    5455             :         A::l            ambiguous (in D and E)
    5456             :         A::f()          A::f()
    5457             :         A::g(1)         B::g(int)
    5458             :         A::g('x')       C::g(char)
    5459             :         A::g(2.0)       ambiguous (B::g or C::g.  D::g is hidden)
    5460             : 
    5461             : inline_namespace_only is TRUE if a symbol was found in a given namespace
    5462             : and that symbol can overload with symbols from inline namespaces (or
    5463             : named in strong using-directives in g++ mode).
    5464             : 
    5465             : If no symbol is found in the specified namespace, NULL is returned.
    5466             : */
    5467             : {
